			/**
			 * This is the failsafe method for finding the default jump height (57.0) by jumping to its location.
			 * If the initial method fails, the plugin will rely on this method instead.
			 *
			 * Note: This method only works on Mac/Windows, since on Linux, it just points to the offset's address not the value's actual address.
			 **/
			"DoJumpValueRead"
			{
				"signature"	"CTerrorGameMovement::DoJump"
				"mac"
				{
					"read"		"209"
				}
				"windows"
				{
					"read"		"174"
				}
				"read"		"0"
			}
		}

			/**
			 * CTankClaw::GroundPound()
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "IsVersusMode" check.
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux/Mac:
			 * 1. Look in the "CTankClaw::GroundPound" function for a variable that stores the return value of "IsVersusMode".
			 * 2. Verify that it starts with "E8" and is 5 bytes long.
			 * 3a. (Linux) Verify that the next line starts with "84" and is 2 bytes long.
			 * 3b. (Mac) Verify that the next two lines each start with "89" and are each 6 bytes long.
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Look in the "CTankClaw::GroundPound" function for a variable assigned to another variable right below a funtion call to "CBaseEntity::GetTeamNumber".
			 * 2. Verify that it starts with "74" and is 2 bytes long.
			 * 3. Verify that the next line starts with "80" and is 5 bytes long.
			 * 4. Verify that the next line starts with "74" and is 2 bytes long.
			 **/
			"CTankClaw::GroundPound::Check"
			{
				"linux"		"1043" // start at E8 and patch 7 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"mac"		"913" // start at E8 and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"windows"	"761" // start at 74 and patch 9 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
			}

			/**
			 * CTankClaw::SweepFist(Vector const&, Vector const&)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "IsVersusMode" check.
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Look in the "CTankClaw::SweepFist" function for a condition that validates "IsVersusMode" or "IsHoldoutMode".
			 * 2. Verify that it starts with "E8" and is 5 bytes long.
			 * 3. The instruction should look like a function call.
			 **/
			"CTankClaw::SweepFist::Check1"
			{
				"linux"		"1052" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"mac"		"2869" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"windows"	"1067" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
			}

			/**
			 * CTankClaw::SweepFist(Vector const&, Vector const&)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "IsHoldoutMode" check.
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Look in the "CTankClaw::SweepFist" function for a condition that validates "IsVersusMode" or "IsHoldoutMode".
			 * 2. Verify that it starts with "E8" and is 5 bytes long.
			 * 3. The instruction should look like a function call.
			 **/
			"CTankClaw::SweepFist::Check2"
			{
				"linux"		"3424" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"mac"		"2878" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"windows"	"1076" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
			}

			/**
			 * CTankRock::OnRelease(Vector const&, QAngle const&, Vector const&, Vector const&)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "CBaseEntity::EmitSound" call for "HulkZombie.Throw.FlyLoop".
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux/Mac:
			 * 1. Locate the "HulkZombie.Throw.FlyLoop" string.
			 * 2. The instruction should look like a function call.
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Locate the "HulkZombie.Throw.FlyLoop" string.
			 * 2. The instruction should look like a function call.
			 * 3. Look for the 2-byte float (FLDZ) instruction right before a PUSH instruction above that function call.
			 * 4. The length of the JMP instruction patch will be determined by the following equation:
			 * Let a1 = Address of the patch location + two bytes (because the patch itself takes two bytes)
			 * Let a2 = Address of the start of the setup for the "CBaseEntity::ThinkSet" call
			 * Equation: a2 - a1 = JMP instruction length
			 **/
			"CTankRock::OnRelease::SoundLoop"
			{
				"linux"		"182" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"mac"		"206" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"windows"	"117" // start at D9 and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
			}

			/**
			 * CTerrorGameRules::GetMissionFirstMap(KeyValues**)
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Locate the "Game/chapter" string.
			 * 2. The instruction should be a push instruction.
			 * 3. The offset will refer to the byte before the start of the string's push instruction.
			 **/
			"CTerrorGameRules::GetMissionFirstMap::Push"

				"windows"	"65"

			 * CTerrorGun::EquipSecondWeapon()
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "CTerrorGun::Deploy" function call.
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Look for the fourth "CBaseCombatCharacter::GetActiveWeapon" function call.
			 * 2. The call instruction below that should be the start of the "CTerrorGun::Holster" function call.
			 * 3. The call instruction below that should be the start of the "CBaseCombatCharacter::SetActiveWeapon" function call.
			 * 4. The call instruction below that should be the start of the "CTerrorGun::Deploy" function call.
			 * 5. The length of the JMP instruction patch will be determined by the following equation:
			 * Let a1 = Address of the patch location + two bytes (because the patch itself takes two bytes)
			 * Let a2 = Address of the start of the instruction after the "CTerrorGun::Deploy" call instruction
			 * Equation: a2 - a1 = JMP instruction length
			 **/
			"CTerrorGun::EquipSecondWeapon::Deploy" // JMP instruction
			{
				"linux"		"325" // start at 8B and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"mac"		"405" // start at 8B and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"windows"	"425" // start at 8B and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction

			 * 4. Compare your dump's offsets with asherkin's dump's offsets to find the target function.

			 * 2b. (Mac) The byte pattern can be found in the "CTraceBulletEntityEnumerator::PerformMultiTrace" function.
			 * 3. The byte pattern should be a MOV instruction and can only be found once in this function.
			 * 4. The patch location starts at the fifth byte.
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Search for the "68 03 40 00 02" byte pattern.
			 * 2. The byte pattern can be found in the "CTraceBulletEntityEnumerator::PerformMultiTrace" function.
			 * 3. The byte pattern should be a PUSH instruction and can only be found once in this function.
			 * 4. The patch location starts at the second byte.
			 **/

			{

				"mac"		"103" // start at 03 and patch 4 bytes with "00 00 00 02"
				"windows"	"63" // start at 03 and patch 4 bytes with "00 00 00 02"
			}

			 * 2. The byte pattern can be found in the "TraceBullet" function.

			 * 4. The patch location starts at the sixth byte.

			 * 2. The byte pattern can be found in the "CTraceBulletEntityEnumerator::PerformMultiTrace" function.

			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Search for the "FF ? 84 C0 75" byte pattern.
			 * 2. The byte pattern can be found in the "CTraceBulletEntityEnumerator::PerformMultiTrace" function.

				"windows"	"222" // start at 75 and patch 2 bytes with "90 90"

			/**
			 * Tank::GetIntentionInterface()
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux/Mac:
			 * 1. Locate the function.
			 * 2. Multiply the member variable offset by 4.
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Find the function's offsets with asherkin's VTable dump.
			 * 2. In IDA Pro, go to the ".rdata" section of the Windows binary.
			 * 3. Search for "Tank::`vftable'" to jump to the "Tank" vtable.
			 * 4. Compare your dump's offsets with asherkin's dump's offsets to find the target function.
			 * 5. Look for the target function in the target binary.
			 * 6. Multiply the member variable offset by 4.
			 **/
			"Tank::GetIntentionInterface::Intention"
			{
				"linux"		"11940"
				"mac"		"11940"
				"windows"	"11924"
			}

			/**
			 * TankAttack::TryToThrowRock(Tank *)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the first condition for choosing between punching and throw a rock.
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux:
			 * 1. Look for the six-byte jump (JNZ) instruction under the first call to the "GetDifficulty" function.
			 * 2. The instruction refers to the if statement that determines whether the Tank should be punch or throw a rock.
			 *
			 * How to find on Mac/Windows:
			 * 1. Look for the two-byte jump (JZ) instruction under the first call to the "GetDifficulty" function.
			 * 2. The instruction refers to the if statement that determines whether the Tank should be punch or throw a rock.
			 **/
			"TankAttack::TryToThrowRock::GetDifficulty"
			{
				"linux"		"133" // start at "0F 85" and patch the "85" with "8D" to always force the jump to the next instruction.
				"mac"		"64" // start at 74 and patch 1 byte with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"windows"	"48" // start at 75 and patch 1 byte with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
			}

			/**
			 * TankAttack::TryToThrowRock(Tank *)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the second condition for choosing between punching and throw a rock.
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux:
			 * 1. Look for the six-byte jump (JNZ) instruction under the first call to the "GetDifficulty" function.
			 * 2. The instruction refers to the second call to the "GetDifficulty" function.
			 *
			 * How to find on Mac/Windows:
			 * 1. Look for the two-byte jump (JNZ) instruction under the first call to the "GetDifficulty" function.
			 * 2. The instruction refers to the second call to the "GetDifficulty" function.
			 **/
			"TankAttack::TryToThrowRock::GetDifficulty2"
			{
				"linux"		"1514" // start at "0F 85" and patch the "85" with "8D" to always force the jump to the next instruction.
				"mac"		"74" // start at 74 and patch 1 byte with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"windows"	"58" // start at 75 and patch 1 byte with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
			}

			/**
			 * TankBehavior::InitialContainedAction(Tank *)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the condition for choosing between attack mode and idle state.
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux/Mac:
			 * 1. Look for the third two-byte jump (JZ) instruction.
			 * 2. The instruction refers to the if statement that determines whether the Tank should be in attack mode or idle state.
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Look for the fourth two-byte jump (JNZ) instruction.
			 * 2. The instruction refers to the if statement that determines whether the Tank should be in attack mode or idle state.
			 **/
			"TankBehavior::InitialContainedAction::Condition" // JMP instruction
			{
				"linux"		"101" // start at 74 and patch 2 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"mac"		"98" // start at 74 and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"windows"	"49" // start at 75 and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
			}

		"Addresses"
		{
			/**
			 * Windows: Uses an offset of "CDirectorMusicBanks::OnRoundStart" to get the Director's address.
			 * Linux/Mac: Uses a symbol pointing to the Director's address.
			 **/
			"CDirector"
			{
				"linux"
				{
					"signature"	"TheDirector"
				}
				"mac"
				{
					"signature"	"TheDirector"
				}
				"windows"
				{
					"signature"	"CDirectorMusicBanks::OnRoundStart"
					"read"		"12"
				}
				"read"		"0"
			}

			/**
			 * This is the failsafe method for finding the default jump height (57.0) by jumping to its location.
			 * If the initial method fails, the plugin will rely on this method instead.
			 **/
			"DoJumpValueRead"
			{
				"signature"	"CTerrorGameMovement::DoJump"
				"linux"
				{
					"read"		"671"
				}
				"mac"
				{
					"read"		"231"
				}
				"windows"
				{
					"read"		"86"
				}
				"read"		"0"
			}
		}

			/**
			 * CSpitterProjectile::Create(Vector const&, QAngle const&, Vector const&, Vector const&, CBaseCombatCharacter*)
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Locate the "Spitter projectile spawned at %f %f %f, velocity %f %f %f\n" string.
			 * 2. The instruction should be a push instruction.

			 **/
			"CSpitterProjectile::Create::Push"
			{
				"windows"	"74"
			}

			/**
			 * CTankClaw::GroundPound()
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "HasPlayerControlledZombies" check.
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux:
			 * 1. Look in the "CTankClaw::GroundPound" function for a variable that stores the return value of "HasPlayerControlledZombies".
			 * 2. Look for a condition that validates that variable.
			 * 3. Verify that it starts with "0F" and is 6 bytes long.
			 *
			 * How to find on Mac:
			 * 1. Look in the "CTankClaw::GroundPound" function for a variable that stores the return value of "HasPlayerControlledZombies".
			 * 2. Verify that it starts with "E8" and is 5 bytes long.
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Look in the "CTankClaw::GroundPound" function for a variable that stores the return value of "HasPlayerControlledZombies".
			 * 2. Look for a condition that validates that variable.
			 * 3. Verify that it starts with "74" and is 2 bytes long.
			 * 4. Verify that the next line starts with "80" and is 4 bytes long.
			 * 5. Verify that the next line starts with "74" and is 2 bytes long.
			 **/
			"CTankClaw::GroundPound::Check"
			{
				"linux"		"988" // start at 0F and patch 2 bytes with NOP (0x90) and an unconditional jump (0xE9) to skip instruction
				"mac"		"962" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"windows"	"923" // start at 74 and patch 8 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
			}

			/**
			 * CTankClaw::SweepFist(Vector const&, Vector const&)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "HasPlayerControlledZombies" check.
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Look in the "CTankClaw::SweepFist" function for a condition that validates "HasPlayerControlledZombies" or "IsSurvivalMode".
			 * 2. Verify that it starts with "E8" and is 5 bytes long.
			 * 3. The instruction should look like a function call.
			 **/
			"CTankClaw::SweepFist::Check1"
			{
				"linux"		"2554" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"mac"		"2923" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"windows"	"1382" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
			}

			/**
			 * CTankClaw::SweepFist(Vector const&, Vector const&)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "IsSurvivalMode" check.
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Look in the "CTankClaw::SweepFist" function for a condition that validates "HasPlayerControlledZombies" or "IsSurvivalMode".
			 * 2. Verify that it starts with "E8" and is 5 bytes long.
			 * 3. The instruction should look like a function call.
			 **/
			"CTankClaw::SweepFist::Check2"
			{
				"linux"		"3488" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"mac"		"2932" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"windows"	"1391" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
			}

			/**
			 * CTankRock::OnRelease(Vector const&, QAngle const&, Vector const&, Vector const&)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "CBaseEntity::EmitSound" call for "HulkZombie.Throw.FlyLoop".
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux/Mac:
			 * 1. Locate the "HulkZombie.Throw.FlyLoop" string.
			 * 2. The instruction should look like a function call.
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Locate the "HulkZombie.Throw.FlyLoop" string.
			 * 2. The instruction should look like a function call.
			 * 3. Look for the 2-byte float (FLDZ) instruction right before a PUSH instruction above that function call.
			 * 4. The length of the JMP instruction patch will be determined by the following equation:
			 * Let a1 = Address of the patch location + two bytes (because the patch itself takes two bytes)
			 * Let a2 = Address of the start of the setup for the "CBaseEntity::ThinkSet" call
			 * Equation: a2 - a1 = JMP instruction length
			 **/
			"CTankRock::OnRelease::SoundLoop" // "HulkZombie.Throw.FlyLoop"
			{
				"linux"		"203" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"mac"		"212" // start at E8 and patch 5 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"windows"	"122" // start at D9 and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
			}

			/**
			 * CTerrorGun::EquipSecondWeapon()
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "CTerrorGun::Deploy" function call.
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Look for the fourth "CBaseCombatCharacter::GetActiveWeapon" function call.
			 * 2. The call instruction below that should be the start of the "CTerrorGun::Holster" function call.
			 * 3. The call instruction below that should be the start of the "CBaseCombatCharacter::SetActiveWeapon" function call.
			 * 4. The call instruction below that should be the start of the "CTerrorGun::Deploy" function call.
			 * 5. The length of the JMP instruction patch will be determined by the following equation:
			 * Let a1 = Address of the patch location + two bytes (because the patch itself takes two bytes)
			 * Let a2 = Address of the start of the instruction after the "CTerrorGun::Deploy" call instruction
			 * Equation: a2 - a1 = JMP instruction length
			 **/
			"CTerrorGun::EquipSecondWeapon::Deploy" // JMP instruction
			{
				"linux"		"325" // start at 8B and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"mac"		"475" // start at 8B and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"windows"	"392" // start at 8B and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
			}

			/**
			 * CTerrorGun::EquipSecondWeapon()
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the "CTerrorGun::Holster" function call.

			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Look for the fourth "CBaseCombatCharacter::GetActiveWeapon" function call.
			 * 2. The call instruction below that should be the start of the "CTerrorGun::Holster" function call.
			 * 3. The length of the JMP instruction patch will be determined by the following equation:
			 * Let a1 = Address of the patch location + two bytes (because the patch itself takes two bytes)
			 * Let a2 = Address of the start of the instruction after the "CTerrorGun::Holster" call instruction
			 * Equation: a2 - a1 = JMP instruction length
			 **/
			"CTerrorGun::EquipSecondWeapon::Holster" // JMP instruction
			{
				"linux"		"294" // start at 8B and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"mac"		"444" // start at 8B and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
				"windows"	"370" // start at 8B and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
			}

			 * 2. The call instruction below that should be the start of the "CTerrorGun::Holster" function call.
			 * 3. The call instruction below that should be the start of the "CBaseCombatCharacter::SetActiveWeapon" function call.
			 * 4. The length of the JMP instruction patch will be determined by the following equation:
			 * Let a1 = Address of the patch location + two bytes (because the patch itself takes two bytes)

			/**
			 * CTerrorPlayer::Event_Killed(CTakeDamageInfo const&)
			 *
			 * Note: This is the offset for the "m_hAttacker" member variable in the "CTakeDamageInfo" class.
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Look in the alliedmodders/hl2sdk-l4d2 "takedamageinfo.h" file.
			 * 2. Each member variable takes up 4 bytes for each of its cells (12 bytes for floats).

			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Locate the "insect_swarm" string.
			 * 2. Scroll up until you reach the if statement that checks for the Spitter class (4).
			 * 3a. (Windows) The patch location should be a MOV instruction two lines before a 2-byte CALL instruction.
			 * 3b. (Linux) The patch location should be a MOV instruction three lines before a 6-byte CALL instruction.
			 * 4. The length of the JMP instruction patch will be determined by the following equation:
			 * Let a1 = Address of the patch location + five bytes (because the patch itself takes five bytes)
			 * Let a2 = Address of the start of the setup for the "CBaseEntity::EmitSound" call for "SpitterZombie.Death"
			 * Equation: a2 - a1 = JMP instruction length
			 **/
			"CTerrorPlayer::Event_Killed::SpitterPuddle" // JMP instruction

				"linux"		"12526" // start at 8B and patch 5 bytes with an unconditional jump (0xE9) to skip instruction
				"mac"		"10068" // start at 8B and patch 5 bytes with an unconditional jump (0xE9) to skip instruction
				"windows"	"9332" // start at 8B and patch 5 bytes with an unconditional jump (0xE9) to skip instruction
			}

			/**
			 * CTerrorPlayer::GetFlowDistance(CNavArea const*)
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux/Mac:
			 * 1. Locate the function.
			 * 2. Look for the 9-byte move (MOVSS) instruction.
			 * 3. The offset at the very end of that line of code is the offset for "m_flow".
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Find the function's offsets with asherkin's VTable dump.
			 * 2. In IDA Pro, go to the ".rdata" section of the Windows binary.
			 * 3. Search for "CTerrorPlayer::`vftable'" to jump to the "CTerrorPlayer" vtable.
			 * 4. Compare your dump's offsets with asherkin's dump's offsets to find the target function.
			 * 5. Look for the target function in the Windows binary.
			 * 6. Look for the 7-byte float (FLD) instruction.
			 * 7. The offset at the very end of that line of code is the offset for "m_flow".
			 **/
			"CTerrorPlayer::GetFlowDistance::m_flow"
			{
				"linux"		"340"
				"mac"		"340"
				"windows"	"332"
			}

			 * TankBehavior::InitialContainedAction(Tank *)
			 *
			 * Note: Patches the condition for choosing between attack mode and idle state.
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux/Mac:
			 * 1. Look for the first two-byte jump (JZ) instruction.
			 * 2. The instruction refers to the if statement that determines whether the Tank should be in attack mode or idle state.
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Look for the first two-byte jump (JNZ) instruction.
			 * 2. The instruction refers to the if statement that determines whether the Tank should be in attack mode or idle state.
			 **/
			"TankBehavior::InitialContainedAction::Condition" // condition
			{
				"linux"		"23" // start at 74 and patch 2 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"mac"		"32" // start at 75 and patch 2 bytes with NOPs (0x90)
				"windows"	"16" // start at 75 and patch 2 bytes with a short jump (0xEB) to skip instruction
			}

			/**
			 * TankIdle::GetName()
			 *
			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Use asherkin's VTable dump.
			 **/
			"TankIdle::GetName"
			{
				"linux"		"41"
				"mac"		"41"
				"windows"	"40"
			}

			/**
			 * TraceBullet(BulletGroupTraceInfo_t const&, Vector const&, CTraceFilterSimpleList &)
			 *
			 * How to find on Linux/Mac:
			 * 1. Search for the "C7 ? ? 08 0B 40 00 02" byte pattern.
			 * 2. The byte pattern can be found in the "CTerrorPlayer::FireBullet" function.
			 * 3. The byte pattern should be a MOV instruction and can only be found once in this function.
			 * 4. The patch location starts at the fifth byte.
			 *
			 * How to find on Windows:
			 * 1. Search for the "68 0B 40 00 02" byte pattern.
			 * 2. The byte pattern can be found in the "TraceBullet" function.
			 * 3. The byte pattern should be a PUSH instruction and can only be found once in this function.
			 * 4. The patch location starts at the second byte.
			 **/
			"TraceBullet::Filter"
			{
				"linux"		"9440" // start at 0B and patch 4 bytes with "00 00 00 02"
				"mac"		"8153" // start at 0B and patch 4 bytes with "00 00 00 02"
				"windows"	"2138" // start at 0B and patch 4 bytes with "00 00 00 02"
			}

			 * WitchLocomotion::IsAreaTraversable(CNavArea const*)

			 * 3. The offset in that instruction is the offset for "m_attributeFlags".

			 * How to find:
			 * 1. Find the function's offsets with asherkin's VTable dump.
			 * 2. In IDA Pro, go to the ".rdata" section of the Windows binary.
			 * 3. Search for "WitchLocomotion::`vftable'" to jump to the "WitchLocomotion" vtable.
			 * 4. Compare your dump's offsets with asherkin's dump's offsets to find the target function.

			 * 7. The offset in that instruction is the offset for "m_attributeFlags".
			 **/
